They concluded that the risks to public health from exposure to emissions from shale gas extraction are low if operations are properly run and regulated."<sup id="cite_ref-BEISGuidance2017_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BEISGuidance2017-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Public Health England\'s Dr John Harrison, Director for Radiation, Chemical and Environmental Hazards, stated that: "Where potential risks have been identified in other countries, the reported problems are typically due to operational failure. Good on-site management and appropriate regulation of all aspects of exploratory drilling, gas capture as well as the use and storage of hydraulic fracturing fluid is essential to minimise the risks to the environment and health."<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2015 the health charity <a href="/wiki/Medact" class="mw-redirect" title="Medact">Medact</a> published a paper written by two public health specialists called \'Health &amp; Fracking - The impacts and opportunity costs\', which reviewed health impacts of hydraulic fracturing and suggested a moratorium until a more detailed health and environmental impact assessment could be completed.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> UKOOG criticised Medact\'s understanding of UK regulations and said they had not declared that one of its consultants, who was standing for parliament in the 2015 general election, had a <a href="/wiki/Conflict_of_interest" title="Conflict of interest">conflict of interest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a> journalist Ben Webster also criticised Medact for not declaring one of their consultant\'s conflict of interest and reported that the Medact director had not realised that this consultant was also an anti-fracking candidate.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> MedAct published a response to these criticisms.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The content of the Medact Report 2015 was referred to by many objectors in the June 2015 Public reports pack for the Lancashire County Council Development Control Committee. Lancashire County Council were uncertain how much weight to attach to the Medact report due to "questions from some quarters" about the objectivity of the report based on association of two its contributors with campaigns relating to shale gas.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2016, Medact released an updated public health report,<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> citing health risks from shale gas development and calling upon the government to "abandon its shale gas plans".<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="The_.27Fracking.27_debate"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_\'Fracking\'_debate">The \'Fracking\' debate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydraulic_fracturing_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: The &#039;Fracking&#039; debate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Balcombe_anti_frack_protest.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Balcombe_anti_frack_protest.jpg/220px-Balcombe_anti_frack_protest.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Balcombe_anti_frack_protest.jpg/330px-Balcombe_anti_frack_protest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Balcombe_anti_frack_protest.jpg/440px-Balcombe_anti_frack_protest.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Balcombe_anti_frack_protest.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>18 August 2013: Fracking protest south of Balcombe, Sussex, England.</div></div></div>\n<p>Hydraulic fracturing, "or \'fracking\' as it has become commonly known, is a big issue for local authorities and communities across the country"<sup id="cite_ref-PNAS2016_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PNAS2016-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> and has become part of the <a href="/wiki/Climate_Change" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate Change">Climate Change</a> debate.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Concerns about hydraulic fracturing have been raised across the United Kingdom, including: <a href="/wiki/Balcombe" title="Balcombe">Sussex</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bath_Somerset" class="mw-redirect" title="Bath Somerset">Somerset</a> and <a href="/wiki/Woodnesborough" title="Woodnesborough">Kent</a> in <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, and; the <a href="/wiki/Vale_of_Glamorgan" title="Vale of Glamorgan">Vale of Glamorgan</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_26Sep2011_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_26Sep2011-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Collins_9Dec2011_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collins_9Dec2011-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, <a href="/wiki/Bath_and_North_East_Somerset_Council" title="Bath and North East Somerset Council">Bath and North East Somerset Council</a> voiced concerns that hydraulic fracturing could contaminate <a href="/wiki/Roman_Baths_(Bath)" title="Roman Baths (Bath)">Bath\'s famous hot springs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_28Sep2011a_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_28Sep2011a-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Protests have been held against onshore unconventional fossil fuel exploration that may lead to hydraulic fracturing.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, industry assurances were tarnished when Cuadrilla came under fire for its categorical denials of its plans for hydraulic fracturing near Balcombe after documents from parent company AJ Lucas materialised appearing to indicate the opposite.<sup id="cite_ref-gdib_13Jan2012_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gdib_13Jan2012-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, a Cuadrilla scrapped its plans to frack at Balcombe.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> In May 2014, a letter to the Department of Energy and Climate Change dated June 2011 emerged, confirming the company believed that to achieve commercial production, "significant amounts of hydraulic fracturing" would be required at Balcombe.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Opposition_and_support_for_fracking">Opposition and support for fracking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydraulic_fracturing_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Opposition and support for fracking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There are a number of anti-fracking groups,<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_28Sep2011b_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_28Sep2011b-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\nwhich range from the nationwide <a href="/wiki/Frack_Off" title="Frack Off">Frack Off</a>, which was engaged in the <a href="/wiki/Balcombe_drilling_protest" title="Balcombe drilling protest">Balcombe drilling protest</a>, to local groups such as Residents Action on Fylde Fracking,<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Ribble Estuary Against Fracking,<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> NO Fracking in Sussex, Frack Free Fernhurst<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> and The Vale Says No!<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Environmental <a href="/wiki/NGO" class="mw-redirect" title="NGO">NGOs</a> <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">World Wide Fund for Nature</a> (WWF) and <a href="/wiki/Friends_of_the_Earth" title="Friends of the Earth">Friends of the Earth</a> are also against fracking.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Anti-fracking campaigners say that there are various problems associated with the process including pressure on local transport infrastructure, air and water pollution, the amounts of water used, and potential economic damage to agricultural, food production and tourism industries.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Pro-fracking campaigners such as the <a href="/wiki/Centrica" title="Centrica">Centrica</a>-backed group North West Energy Task Force say the "fracking industry" "could bring a boost to jobs and the economy" and that "shale gas has a pivotal role to play in the region\'s future success" and "would act as a catalyst to bring the vital investment necessary to secure existing industries and develop new ones."<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Advertising_Standards_Authority_complaints">Advertising Standards Authority complaints</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydraulic_fracturing_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Advertising Standards Authority complaints">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Anti-fracking and pro-fracking campaigners have submitted a series of complaints about advertisements, brochures and leaflets to the Advertising Standards Agency.\n</p><p>In April 2013, "fracking activist" <a href="/wiki/Refracktion" title="Refracktion">Refracktion</a> reported Cuadrilla\'s brochure to the <a href="/wiki/Advertising_Standards_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Advertising Standards Authority (United Kingdom)">Advertising Standards Authority</a> (ASA), who deemed that of the 18 statements made, 11 were acceptable and six had breached the Committee of Advertising Practice (CAP) code,<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> and that the brochure "must not appear again in its present form".<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> In January 2015 Reverend Michael Roberts and Ken Wilkinson reported an anti-fracking group\'s leaflet to the ASA. The ASA resolved the complaint with an informal ruling that the group, Residents Action On Fylde Fracking (RAFF), had "exaggerated the size and scale of planned fracking operations".<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> RAFF "agreed to amend or withdraw advertising without the need for a formal investigation".<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, Cuadrilla and Reverend Michael Roberts reported a leaflet produced by Friends of the Earth to the ASA<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Fundraising_Standards_Board" class="mw-redirect" title="Fundraising Standards Board">Fundraising Standards Board</a> (FRSB), now known as the <a href="/wiki/Fundraising_Standards_Board" class="mw-redirect" title="Fundraising Standards Board">Fundraising Regulator</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> Friends of the Earth gave assurance to the ASA that they would not repeat claims in their advertisements about "the effects of fracking on the health of local populations, drinking water or property prices" "in the absence of adequate evidence".<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> The ASA clarified their position,<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> after it became evident that FoE rejected the results of their investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="Needs a third-party reliable source to be able to claim that &#39;it became evident that FoE rejected the results&#39; (March 2016)">not in citation given</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (March 2016)">original research?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wales">Wales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydraulic_fracturing_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Wales">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In October 2011 the campaign to prohibit Coastal Oil and Gas from test drilling at the Llandow Industrial Estate, in the Vale of Glamorgan, met with initial success after local councillors unanimously refused the company\'s plans, though Coastal immediately indicated it would appeal.<sup id="cite_ref-Collins_21Oct2011_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collins_21Oct2011-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Residents feared that successful exploration would be the prelude for hydraulic fracturing.<sup id="cite_ref-Collins_9Dec2011_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collins_9Dec2011-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> The basis of the Council\'s decision was a letter from <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Water" title="Welsh Water">Welsh Water</a> stating that there was "a very small risk" of contamination of its reserve groundwater sites from exploratory drilling.<sup id="cite_ref-Collins_22Oct2012_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collins_22Oct2012-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The rejection came despite the Council being told that, strictly from a planning point of view, there were no "reasonable or sustainable grounds" to refuse, and despite the drilling application containing no explicit mention of hydraulic fracturing. The company had additionally claimed that, since the "gas shales in the Vale are not as thick as elsewhere", any discoveries would be "very unlikely" to require hydraulic fracturing for extraction.<sup id="cite_ref-Collins_21Oct2011_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collins_21Oct2011-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Coastal Oil and Gas decided to appeal to the Welsh Government, rather than undertake legal action against the local authority,<sup id="cite_ref-Collins_25Nov2011_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collins_25Nov2011-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/Public_enquiry" class="mw-redirect" title="Public enquiry">public enquiry</a> began in May 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Collins_27Feb2012_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collins_27Feb2012-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Coastal\'s chances of success at the enquiry were boosted by <a href="/wiki/Kent_County_Council" title="Kent County Council">Kent County Council</a> approval of the company\'s near-identical plans for preliminary drilling in Woodnesborough,<sup id="cite_ref-Collins_9Dec2011_146-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collins_9Dec2011-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> and were increased to near certainty after Welsh Water effectively retracted its previous risk assessment.<sup id="cite_ref-Collins_27Feb2012_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collins_27Feb2012-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><br />\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry_response">Industry response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydraulic_fracturing_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Industry response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In arguing its case, Cuadrilla contrasts its approach with the one taken in the United States, claiming that only three chemicals\xe2\x80\x94a polyacrylamide lubricant commonly found in cosmetics, hydrochloric acid, and a biocide used to purify drinking water\xe2\x80\x94will be used in the UK, compared with the hundreds that can be used across the Atlantic; that it has invested in more expensive, better equipment than that used by companies operating in the US;<sup id="cite_ref-Harvey_20Apr2011_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harvey_20Apr2011-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> that its wells have three layers of pipe casing to line the wells, whereas many American ones only have two; that the barrier between the gas escaping up the pipe and ground water is thicker; that cement will be returned to the surface, blocking identified leak paths; and that drilling fluids will be collected in closed steel tanks, rather than in lined earthen pits, as often happens in the States.<sup id="cite_ref-Rayment_23Oct2011_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rayment_23Oct2011-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Harvey_20Apr2011b_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harvey_20Apr2011b-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> According to Cuadrilla\'s communication advisor, "<a href="/wiki/Gasland" title="Gasland">Gasland</a> (the US documentary about shale gas) really changed everything. .&#160;.&#160;. Before that, shale gas was not seen as routinely controversial."<sup id="cite_ref-Harvey_20Apr2011_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harvey_20Apr2011-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Effect_on_house_prices">Effect on house prices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydraulic_fracturing_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Effect on house prices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In August 2014, a report called \'Shale Gas:Rural Economic Impacts\' was published by the UK Government, in response to a Freedom of Information request, from <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a>. It was due for publication in March 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>  It was notable as large parts of this had been redacted, leading to criticism about the transparency of information being provided.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Lancashire \'North West Energy Task Force\', a body that broadly supports the extraction of shale gas,  commissioned a report on the effect of house prices in the area surrounding the Preese Hall 1 well, after the seismic issues lead to a suspension of activity by the drilling company, Cuadrilla. The report concluded that "Taken together, there is no clear evidence based on this data to suggest that onshore gas operations have had a material impact on local house prices" <sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2017, Friends of the Earth were instructed not to repeat claims about "plummeting house prices" after complaints and an investigation by the Advertising Standards Authority <sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydraulic_fracturing_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Cost_of_electricity_by_source" title="Cost of electricity by source">Cost of electricity by source</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Oil_and_gas_industry_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Oil and gas industry in the United Kingdom">Oil and gas industry in the United Kingdom</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Refracktion" title="Refracktion">Refracktion</a>, an environmental organisation</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydraulic_fracturing_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 25em; href="#cite_ref-OOGSG1_27-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-OOGSG1_27-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-OOGSG1_27-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span Environment Agency. 17 August 2016<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">3 September</span> 2016</span>. <q>Flowback fluid can be treated and re-used as fresh injection fluid for the purpose of hydraulic fracturing and we consider this to be a suitable environmental option. Flowback fluid must be reused where it is reasonably practicable to do so to meet the MWD obligation to minimise waste. However, waste flowback fluid may contain a concentration of NORM radionuclide\'s above the out of scope values. It will then require a radioactive substances activity permit for its disposal. You must send this to an appropriate permitted waste facility for treatment or disposal</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Onshore+Oil+%26+Gas+Sector+Guidance+Version+1%2C+17+August+2016&amp;rft.pub=Environment+Agency&amp;rft.date=2016-08-17&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.gov.uk%2Fgovernment%2Fuploads%2Fsystem%2Fuploads%2Fattachment_data%2Ffile%2F545924%2FLIT_10495.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHydraulic+fracturing+in+the+United+Kingdom" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-NORM_TreatDisp-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-NORM_TreatDisp_28-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation report">"4.7". <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.gov.uk/government/uploads/system/uploads/attachment_data/file/335821/Final_strategy_NORM.pdf">Strategy for the management of Naturally Occurring Radioactive Material (NORM) waste in the United Kingdom</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> (Report). p.&#160;30<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2 September</span> 2016</span>. <q>Treatment and disposal may take place by re-injection during subsequent hydraulic fracturing, or it may be carried out at sites remote from the shale gas production facilities, for example sewage or effluent treatment sites and would be expected to remove up to 90% of NORM; only very low levels would still remain. After treatment, the water may still retain some of this natural radioactivity and disposal to rivers, estuaries, sea or groundwater may lead to intakes of radioactivity through consumption of drinking water and contaminated foodstuffs, or by direct exposure pathways.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=report&amp;rft.btitle=Strategy+for+the+management+of+Naturally+Occurring+Radioactive+Material+%28NORM%29+waste+in+the+United+Kingdom&amp;rft.pages=30&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.gov.uk%2Fgovernment%2Fuploads%2Fsystem%2Fuploads%2Fattachment_data%2Ffile%2F335821%2FFinal_strategy_NORM.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHydraulic+fracturing+in+the+United+Kingdom" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-GreenStylesBaptie-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-GreenStylesBaptie_29-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation report">Green, Dr Christopher A.; Styles, Professor Peter; Baptie, Dr Brian J. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">28 March</span> 2017</span>. <q>The fracturing fluid that Cuadrilla has used at the Preese Hall exploration well site, and plans to use at future exploration well sites, is composed almost entirely of fresh water and sand.  Cuadrilla also has approval to use the following additives: Polyacrylamide (friction reducer) Sodium salt (for tracing fracturing fluid) Hydrochloric acid (diluted with water) Glutaraldehyde biocide (used to cleanse water and remove bacteria) So far, as additives to fracturing fluid, Cuadrilla has only used polyacrylamide friction reducer along with a minuscule amount of salt, which acts as a tracer. Cuadrilla have not needed to use biocide as the water supplied by United Utilities to their Lancashire exploration well sites has already been treated to remove bacteria, nor have they used diluted hydrochloric acid in fracturing fluid.  Additives proposed, in the quantities proposed, have resulted in the fracturing fluid being classified as non-hazardous by the Environment Agency.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=CHAPTER+1.+Introduction+and+Overview%3A+the+Role+of+Shale+Gas+in+Securing+Our+Energy+Future&amp;rft.pages=1-45&amp;rft.pub=Royal+Society+of+Chemistry&amp;rft.date=2014-01-01&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1039%2F9781782620556-00001&amp;rft.aulast=Hardy&amp;rft.aufirst=Peter&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fpubs.rsc.org%2Fen%2Fcontent%2Fchapterhtml%2F2014%2F9781782620556-00001%3Fisbn%3D978-1-78262-055-6&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHydraulic+fracturing+in+the+United+Kingdom" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Broderick, Dr John; Anderson, Professor Kevin; Wood, Dr Ruth; Gilbert, Dr Paul; Sharmina, Mrs Maria; Footitt, Mr Anthony; Glynn, Dr Steven; Nicholls, Ms Fiona (November 2011). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.mace.manchester.ac.uk/media/eps/schoolofmechanicalaerospaceandcivilengineering/newsandevents/news/research/pdfs2011/shale-gas-threat-report.pdf">"Shale gas: an updated assessment of environmental and climate change impacts"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">22 February</span> 2017</span>. <q>"The maximum reported height of an upward propagating hydraulic fracture from several thousand fracturing operations in the Marcellus, Barnett, Woodford, Eagle Ford and Niobrara shale (USA) is 588 m. Based on these empirical data, the probability of a stimulated hydraulic fracture extending vertically less than 350 m is less than 1%. Constraining the probability of stimulating unusually tall hydraulic fractures in sedimentary rocks is extremely important as an evidence base for decisions on the safe vertical separation between the depth of stimulation and rock strata not intended for penetration".</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Hydraulic+fractures%3A+How+far+can+they+go%3F&amp;rft.pages=1&amp;rft.pub=ReFine&amp;rft.au=Davies&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.refine.org.uk%2Fmedia%2Fsites%2Fresearchwebsites%2F1refine%2Fpapers%2FDavies%2C%25202012%2520-%2520Hydraulic%2520Fractures%2520-%2520how%2520far%2520can%2520they%2520go.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHydraulic+fracturing+in+the+United+Kingdom" class="Z3988"></span><span class="citation-comment" style="display:none; color:#33aa33; margin-left:0.3em">CS1 maint: Explicit use of et al. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">18 October</span> 2014</span>. <q>It is necessary to distinguish between hazardous substances, inputs of which should be prevented, and other pollutants, inputs of which should be limited. Annex VIII to Directive 2000/60/EC, listing the main pollutants relevant for the water environment, should be used to identify hazardous and non-hazardous substances which present an existing or potential risk of pollution.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=eur-lex.europa.eu&amp;rft.atitle=DIRECTIVE+2006%2F118%2FEC+OF+THE+EUROPEAN+PARLIAMENT+AND+OF+THE+COUNCIL+of+12+December+2006+on+the+protection+of+groundwater+against+pollution+and+deterioration&amp;rft.date=2006-12-12&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feur-lex.europa.eu%2Flegal-content%2FEN%2FTXT%2F%3Furi%3DCELEX%3A32006L0118&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHydraulic+fracturing+in+the+United+Kingdom" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-70"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-70">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.wfduk.org/sites/default/files/Media/170116%20Substance%20Determinationsfinal.pdf">"170116 Substance Determinations final"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. DEFRA. p.&#160;15<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">16 March</span> 2017</span>. <q>4.6 The List I and List II groupings of substances under the GWD and 1998 Regulations no longer apply. Substances are instead treated as either \'hazardous substances\' (initially broadly equating to the former List I) or non-hazardous pollutants\' (analogous to the former List II, but potentially applying to all other pollutants) \'Hazardous substance\' is defined in Article 2(29) of the Water FD as meaning substances or groups of substances that are toxic, persistent and liable to bio-accumulate, and other substances or groups of substances which give rise to an equivalent level of concern. The GWDD requires a different approach by which Member States or their competent authorities determine which substances should be determined as hazardous on the basis of their toxicity, persistence and capacity to bio-accumulate \xe2\x80\x93 i.e. positive determination rather than removal from a pre-determined list. This provides greater flexibility to include substances within, or alternatively exclude them from, the \'hazardous\' category. In practice substances which have been determined as List I will continue to be regarded as hazardous and will only be reviewed if new evidence becomes available.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Chapter+4&amp;rft.btitle=Environmental+Permitting+Guidance+Groundwater+Activities&amp;rft.pages=15&amp;rft.pub=DEFRA&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.gov.uk%2Fgovernment%2Fuploads%2Fsystem%2Fuploads%2Fattachment_data%2Ffile%2F69474%2Fpb13555-ep-groundwater-activities-101221.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHydraulic+fracturing+in+the+United+Kingdom" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-72"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-72">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Harvey, Fiona; Vaughan, Adam (10 October 2013). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2013/oct/10/fracking-chemical-balcombe-meeting">"Fracking firm was barred from using chemical, Balcombe meeting told"</a>. <i>The Guardian</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. UKOOG. <q>UK Onshore Oil and Gas, the representative body of the UK\'s onshore oil and gas industry, notes the contribution made by leading conservation charities to the debate on shale gas regulation in their report: "Are We Fit To Frack." Of the 10 recommendations in the report, the vast majority are already in place or are in discussion. We look forward to being able to discuss with the six bodies who contributed to this report about the best way forward so that we ensure all misconceptions about the shale gas industry in the UK can be addressed. Ken Cronin Chief Executive UKOOG commented "We have studied this report and the fact that many of the recommendations are already in place in the UK or are in the process of being put in place. We hope that the publication of this report, despite a number of critical inaccuracies, will kickstart a process of open dialogue which we have already proposed to conservation agencies.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=UKOOG+Fit+to+Frack+response&amp;rft.pub=UKOOG&amp;rft.date=2014-03-14&amp;rft.au=UKOOG&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.ukoog.org.uk%2Fabout-ukoog%2Fpress-releases%2F121-ukoog-fit-to-frack-response&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHydraulic+fracturing+in+the+United+Kingdom" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Harrison-75"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Harrison_75-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation report">Gwen Harrison, Stuart Parkinson and Gary McFarlane (July 2014). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.cieh.org/WorkArea/showcontent.aspx?id=53520">Shale gas and fracking: examining the evidence</a> (Report). Retrieved <span class="nowrap">5 April</span> 2017</span>. <q>the Offshore Installations and Wells (Design and Construction etc) Regulations 1996, known as DCR.  These regulations, include specific requirements for all wells, whether onshore or offshore, and include well integrity provisions which apply throughout the life of shale gas wells. Environment Agency<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">16 March</span> 2017</span>. <q>Water stored below the ground in rocks or other geological strata is called groundwater. The geological strata that hold water are called aquifers. Groundwater may rise to the surface through naturally occurring springs, or be abstracted using boreholes and wells. Groundwater may also naturally flow into rivers (called base flow) and support wetlands, forming part of local ecosystems.The legal definition of groundwater is: \'All water which is below the surface of the ground in the saturation zone and in direct contact with the ground or subsoil.\'Aquifers are: \'A subsurface layer or layers of rock or other geological strata of sufficient porosity and permeability to allow either a significant flow of groundwater or the abstraction of significant quantities of groundwater.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Chapter+2&amp;rft.btitle=Protect+groundwater+and+prevent+groundwater+pollution&amp;rft.pub=Environment+Agency&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.gov.uk%2Fgovernment%2Fpublications%2Fprotect-groundwater-and-prevent-groundwater-pollution%2Fprotect-groundwater-and-prevent-groundwater-pollution&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHydraulic+fracturing+in+the+United+Kingdom" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-105"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-105">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bgs.ac.uk/research/groundwater/shaleGas/methaneBaseline/results.html">BGS Methane Baseline study</a></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-106"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-106">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.raeng.org.uk/publications/reports/shale-gas-extraction-in-the-uk">"Shale gas extraction in the UK: a review of hydraulic fracturing &#124; Summary Recommendation 1"</a>. Royal Academy of engineering<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">5 March</span> 2017</span>. <q>To detect groundwater contamination, the UK\'s environmental regulators should work with the British Geological Survey (BGS) to carry out comprehensive national baseline surveys of methane and other contaminants in groundwater. Operators should carry out site-specific monitoring of methane and other contaminants in groundwater before, during and after shale gas operations</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Shale+gas+extraction+in+the+UK%3A+a+review+of+hydraulic+fracturing+%26%23124%3B+Summary+Recommendation+1&amp;rft.pub=Royal+Academy+of+engineering&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.raeng.org.uk%2Fpublications%2Freports%2Fshale-gas-extraction-in-the-uk&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHydraulic+fracturing+in+the+United+Kingdom" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-107"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-107">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2015/7/section/50">"2015 Infrastructure Act"</a>. Royal Academy of Engineering. p.&#160;37<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">22 February</span> 2017</span>. <q>The very unlikely event of fractures propagating all the way to overlying aquifers would provide a possible route for fracture fluids to flow. However, suitable pressure and permeability conditions would also be necessary for fluids to flow. Sufficiently high upward pressures would be required during the fracturing process and then sustained afterwards over the long term once the fracturing process had ceased. It is very difficult to conceive of how this might occur given the UK\'s shale gas hydrogeological environments. Upward flow of fluids from the zone of shale gas extraction to overlying aquifers via fractures in the intervening strata is highly unlikely</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=RAENG&amp;rft.atitle=Shale+gas+extraction+in+the+UK+A+review+of+hydraulic+fracturing%2C+chapter+4.3.3&amp;rft.pages=37&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.raeng.org.uk%2Fpublications%2Freports%2Fshale-gas-extraction-in-the-uk&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHydraulic+fracturing+in+the+United+Kingdom" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-111"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-111">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Boothroyd, I.M.; Almond, S.; Qassim, S.M.; Worrall, F.; Davies, R.J. Lancashire County Council Development Control Committee. pp.&#160;723\xe2\x80\x93724<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">20 June</span> 2015</span>. <q>PHE did not comment on the Medact report in this document. The Council commented: Many objectors refer to the 2015 report of the public health charity Medact. Medact say the risks and serious nature of the hazards associated with fracking, coupled with the concerns and uncertainties about the regulatory system, indicate that shale gas development should be halted until a more detailed health and environmental impact assessment is undertaken. The Medact report has not produced new epidemiological research but has reviewed published literature and has requested short papers from relevant experts in particular subject areas. It has also interviewed academics and experts. Unfortunately, one of the contributors (contributing to three of the report\'s six chapters \xe2\x80\x93 chapters 2, 4 and 5) has led a high profile campaign in the Fylde related to shale gas. Another contributor to the report (chapter 3) has previously expressed firm views on shale gas and has objected to this application. This has led to questions from some quarters about the report\'s objectivity.In light of these uncertainties it is not clear how much weight the County Council should attach to the report.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Public+reports+pack+23+June+2015&amp;rft.pages=723-724&amp;rft.pub=Lancashire+County+Council+Development+Control+Committee&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fcouncil.lancashire.gov.uk%2Fdocuments%2Fg4919%2FPublic%2520reports%2520pack%252023rd-Jun-2015%252010.00%2520Development%2520Control%2520Committee.pdf%3FT%3D10&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHydraulic+fracturing+in+the+United+Kingdom" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-143"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-143">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.medact.org/2016/resources/reports/shale-gas-production-in-england/">"Shale Gas Production in England \xe2\x80\x93 an updated public health assessment"</a>. Medact<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">27 February</span> 2017</span>. <q>Key points. Hazardous pollutants are produced at all stages of the shale gas production process. The range of pollutants are outlined in the report.  Based on current evidence it is not possible to conclude that there is a strong association between shale gas related pollution and negative local health effects.  However, there is clearly potential for negative health impacts. In particular, there are risks of (i) adverse reproductive outcomes due to exposure to endocrine disrupting chemicals, (ii) risk of respiratory effects resulting from ozone and smog formation, (iii) stress, anxiety and other psycho-social effects arising from actual and perceived social and economic disruption.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Shale+Gas+Production+in+England+%E2%80%93+an+updated+public+health+assessment&amp;rft.pub=Medact&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.medact.org%2F2016%2Fresources%2Freports%2Fshale-gas-production-in-england%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHydraulic+fracturing+in+the+United+Kingdom" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-144"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-144">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Clark, Pilita (7 July 2016). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.ft.com/content/3abc681e-4438-11e6-b22f-79eb4891c97d">"Fracking threatens UK\'s climate change targets, says report: Government\'s advisers on global warming urge industry to adhere to three conditions"</a>. The Financial Times<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">29 December</span> 2016</span>. <q>Separately, a group of medical professionals repeated their call for the UK to abandon its shale gas plans because of the threats it posed to health. Friends of the Earth gave us an assurance to that effect. Unless the evidence changes, that means it mustn\'t repeat in ads claims about the effects of fracking on the health of local populations, drinking water or property prices. Friends of the Earth has said we "dropped the case". That\'s not an accurate reflection of what\'s happened. We thoroughly investigated the complaints we received and closed the case on receipt of the above assurance. Because of that, we decided against publishing a formal ruling, but plainly that\'s not the same thing as "dropping the case". JLL/NorthWest Energy Task Force<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">14 March</span> 2017</span>. <q>From 1995 to 2014, Preese Hall has seen a higher trajectory of house price growth when compared with Lancashire and the North West. Although Preese Hall saw a larger decline in house prices between the application being submitted and implementation than Lancashire and the North West, the area has seen a price growth of 7.5% between onshore gas operations commencing in 2011 and 2014. This compares with the North West seeing a prices increase by 0.2% whereas Lancashire saw a price decline of 4.2%. Taken together, there is no clear evidence based on this data to suggest that onshore gas operations have had a material impact on local house prices. 34% of households within three miles [5&#160;km] of the subject site fall into the category of Affluent Achievers. A further indication of the prosperity in the area is that 71% of households are owner/occupied</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Residential+research+report%3A+The+Impact+of+On-Shore+Gas+Exploration+Activities+on+Local+House+Prices&amp;rft.pub=JLL%2FNorthWest+Energy+Task+Force&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fd3n8a8pro7vhmx.cloudfront.net%2Fnwenergy%2Fpages%2F102%2Fattachments%2Foriginal%2F1429019521%2FJLL_report_-_NWETF_house_prices_%282%29.pdf%3F1429019521&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHydraulic+fracturing+in+the+United+Kingdom" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-181"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-181">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2017/jan/04/friends-of-earth-ticked-off-claims-anti-fracking-leaflet">"Friends of the Earth ticked off over claims in anti-fracking leaflet"</a>. 4 January 2017<span class="reference-accessdate">.
